This has not created a moral panic, but has been seen more as an ongoing social evolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lawfamger_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-lawfamger-180">[180]</a></sup> Cohabitation, divorce rates, lone parents, and people's reluctance to marry or to have children have increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lawfamger_180-1"><a href="#cite_note-lawfamger-180">[180]</a></sup> However, when it comes to family formation and long term cohabitation instead of marriage, there are very strong differences between the regions of former <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> (which was formally Communist). Significantly more children are born out of wedlock in eastern Germany than in western Germany. In 2012, in eastern Germany 61.6% of births were to unmarried women, while in western Germany only 28.4% were.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Panel_data" title="Panel data">longitudinal survey</a> found that union stability was significantly higher for cohabiting mothers in eastern Germany than western Germany, due to differences in German society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-germanypmc_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-germanypmc-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, family dynamics remain conservative. The principal form of partnership is marriage, and extramarital childbearing and long term cohabitation are not widespread. For instance, in 2014 only 8.2% of births were outside of marriage, which is the lowest percentage among the European Union member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Greece" title="Religion in Greece">Religion in Greece</a> plays a very important role in society; it was only in 1983 that <a href="/wiki/Civil_marriage" title="Civil marriage">civil marriage</a> was introduced in the country. The new laws modernized <a href="/wiki/Family_law" title="Family law">family law</a>, abolished <a href="/wiki/Dowry" title="Dowry">dowry</a>, and provided for equal rights for "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legitimacy_(law)" title="Legitimacy (law)">illegitimate</a>" children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> According to a 2008 study: "Greek society still remains conservative and birthing outside marriage, although protected by law, remains in many ways socially unacceptable."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> Despite this, there have been further legal changes providing for a modern "western" outlook on family life, including Law 3719/2008 dealing with family issues, including Article 14 of the law, which reduced the separation period (necessary before a divorce in certain circumstances) from 4 years to 2 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hungary">Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The literature on <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Second_demographic_transition&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Second demographic transition (page does not exist)">second demographic transition</a> argues as well that highly educated women are more prone to engage in cohabitation, although the reasons are different: they are less concerned with respecting the societal norms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> Some scholars argued that cohabitation is very similar to being single in the sense of not giving up independence and personal autonomy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Hungary, cohabitation was an uncommon phenomenon until the late 1980s and it was largely confined to the divorced or widowed individuals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> Among the ethnic groups, Gypsy/Rroma tended to have higher rates of cohabitation, mainly due to their reluctance to register their marriages officially.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Since the 1980s, cohabitation became much more frequent among all ethnic groups and it has been argued to have strongly influenced the decline in fertility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> As of 2014, 47.3% of births were to unmarried women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Magdalen-asylum.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="800" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Magdalen-asylum.jpg/200px-Magdalen-asylum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Magdalen-asylum.jpg/300px-Magdalen-asylum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Magdalen-asylum.jpg/400px-Magdalen-asylum.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Magdalen-asylum.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Irish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magdalene_laundries" title="Magdalene laundries">Magdalene Laundry</a>, c. early 1900s. Women who had sexual relations outside marriage were often sent to Magdalene laundries until the mid-20th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cohabitation in Ireland has increased in recent years, and 36.3% of births were to unmarried women in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> Until a few decades ago, women who had children outside of marriage were severely stigmatized and often detained in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magdalene_laundries" title="Magdalene laundries">Magdalene laundries</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Civil_Partnership_and_Certain_Rights_and_Obligations_of_Cohabitants_Act_2010" title="Civil Partnership and Certain Rights and Obligations of Cohabitants Act 2010">Civil Partnership and Certain Rights and Obligations of Cohabitants Act 2010</a> gives some rights to unmarried cohabitants (under this act same-sex couples can enter into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_partnerships" title="Civil partnerships">civil partnerships</a>, while long term unmarried couples - both heterosexual and same sex - who have not registered their relation have some limited rights and obligations).</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> had a historically strong presence, cohabitation is not as common as in other countries of Europe, yet it has increased in recent years. There are significant regional differences, with non-marital unions being more common in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Italy" title="Northern Italy">North of the country</a> than in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Italy" title="Southern Italy">Southern Italy</a>. A study published in 2006 found that long term cohabitation was still novel to Italy, though more common among young people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> As of 2015, the share of births outside of marriage was 28.7%, but this varied by statistical regions as follows: <a href="/wiki/Central_Italy" title="Central Italy">Central Italy</a> (33.8%), <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Italy" title="Northeast Italy">Northeast Italy</a> (33.1%), <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Italy" title="Northwest Italy">Northwest Italy</a> (31.3%), <a href="/wiki/Insular_Italy" title="Insular Italy">Insular Italy</a> (24.2%), and <a href="/wiki/South_Italy" title="South Italy">South Italy</a> (20.3%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Netherlands">The Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: The Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Dutch researchers have found that research participants see cohabitation as a risk-reduction strategy in a country with high relationship instability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> As of 2014, 48.7% births were to unmarried women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Norway">Norway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Norway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Cohabitation is a common type of partnership in Norway. Cohabitants have some rights if they have joint children, or if they have lived together for five years. Cohabitants can also regulate their relationship through a <a href="/wiki/Cohabitation_agreement" title="Cohabitation agreement">cohabitation agreement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> In Norway, in 2013, 55.2% of children were born outside of marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-europa.eu_151-2"><a href="#cite_note-europa.eu-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Poland, after the fall of Communism, the influence of religion has increased. Indeed, Poland has one of the most religious populations in Europe (see <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Europe" title="Religion in Europe">Religion in Europe</a>). Cohabitation in Poland has traditionally been associated with the lower social classes, but in recent years an increase has been seen among the more educated. Family structure in Poland remains traditional: Marriages are contracted at relatively young ages, and the incidence of divorce is relatively low (by European standards). The exact incidence of cohabitation is not well established, but it is quite low compared to other Western countries. However, Poland is not completely 'immune' to Western influence and, in 2014, 24.2% of children were born outside of marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovakia">Slovakia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Slovakia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Slovakia is more conservative and religious than neighboring Czech Republic. The principal form of partnership is marriage, but extramarital childbearing and cohabitation are slowly spreading, yet this trend is not without criticism; and some view these phenomena as a threat to traditional values.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demographic-research.org_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-demographic-research.org-202">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> In 2014, 38.9% of births were to unmarried women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> Fertility in Slovakia has been described in a 2008 study as "between tradition and modernity".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demographic-research.org_202-1"><a href="#cite_note-demographic-research.org-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Switzerland">Switzerland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Switzerland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="img" style="width: 400px; float: right; clear: right; line-height: 1; text-align: center; background-color: #ffffff; position: relative;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Suisse_cantons.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="744" data-file-width="1052" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Suisse_cantons.svg/400px-Suisse_cantons.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Suisse_cantons.svg/600px-Suisse_cantons.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Suisse_cantons.svg/800px-Suisse_cantons.svg.png 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; background-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.5); padding: 0 2px; left:134px; top:196px"><b><a href="/wiki/Valais" title="Valais">Valais</a></b></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; background-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.5); padding: 0 2px; left:234px; top:180px"><b><a href="/wiki/Ticino" title="Ticino">Ticino</a></b></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; background-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.5); padding: 0 2px; left:298px; top:132px"><b><a href="/wiki/Grisons" title="Grisons">Graubünden<br/>
(Grisons)</a></b></div>

<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; background-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.5); padding: 0 2px; left:222px; top:84px"><b><a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Zug" title="Canton of Zug">Zug</a></b></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; background-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.5); padding: 0 2px; left:90px; top:132px"><b><a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Fribourg" title="Canton of Fribourg">Fribourg</a></b></div>

<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; background-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.5); padding: 0 2px; left:2px; top:68px"><i><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><span style="color: #48A3B5;">France</span></a></i></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; background-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.5); padding: 0 2px; left:218px; top:244px"><i><a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy"><span style="color: #48A3B5;">Italy</span></a></i></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; background-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.5); padding: 0 2px; left:322px; top:88px"><i><a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein"><span style="color: #48A3B5;">Liecht.</span></a></i></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; background-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.5); padding: 0 2px; left:362px; top:72px"><i><a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria"><span style="color: #48A3B5;">Austria</span></a></i></div>
<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; background-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.5); padding: 0 2px; left:302px; top:0px"><i><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany"><span style="color: #48A3B5;">Germany</span></a></i></div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> has a tradition of strong conservatism; which can be seen in its legal and social history: in Europe, Switzerland was one of the last countries to establish gender equality in marriage: married women's rights were severely restricted until 1988, when legal reforms providing gender equality in marriage, abolishing the legal authority of the husband, come into force (these reforms had been approved in 1985 by voters in a <a href="/wiki/Voting_in_Switzerland" title="Voting in Switzerland">referendum</a>, who narrowly voted in favor with 54.7% of voters approving).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adultery" title="Adultery">Adultery</a> was decriminalized in 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Until the late 20th century, most <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Switzerland" title="Cantons of Switzerland">cantons</a> had regulations banning unmarried cohabitation of couples; the last canton to end such prohibition was <a href="/wiki/Valais" title="Valais">Valais</a>, in 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> As of 2015, 22.5% of births were to unmarried women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Births outside marriage are most common in the French speaking part (highest percentage in the cantons of <a href="/wiki/Vaud" title="Vaud">Vaud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Neuch%C3%A2tel" title="Canton of Neuchâtel">Neuchâtel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Geneva" title="Canton of Geneva">Geneva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Jura" title="Canton of Jura">Jura</a>) and least common in the eastern German speaking cantons (lowest percentage in the cantons of <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_St._Gallen" title="Canton of St. Gallen">St. Gallen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Zug" title="Canton of Zug">Zug</a>, <a href="/wiki/Appenzell_Innerrhoden" title="Appenzell Innerrhoden">Appenzell Innerrhoden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Appenzell_Ausserrhoden" title="Appenzell Ausserrhoden">Appenzell Ausserrhoden</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Spanish society has undergone major changes since the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Franco regime</a>. Important legal changes which have occurred throughout the 1970s and 1980s include legalization of <a href="/wiki/Divorce" title="Divorce">divorce</a>, decriminalization of <a href="/wiki/Adultery" title="Adultery">adultery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a> in <a href="/wiki/Family_law" title="Family law">family law</a>, and removing the ban on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contraception" title="Contraception">contraception</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> The liberalization of the political climate has allowed for alternative family formation. In the mid-1990s, cohabitation in Spain was still described as a "marginal" phenomenon, but since the 1990s, cohabitation has increased dramatically in Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> In Spain, in 2015, 44.4% of births were outside of marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> As in other countries, there are regional differences: in 2011, in <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> the figure was 42% - highest in mainland Spain in that year (<a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> 59% and <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> 43.5% were highest) while in <a href="/wiki/Region_of_Murcia" title="Region of Murcia">Murcia</a> it was only 30.7% (lowest).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Russia, many couples express a desire to cohabit before marriage, then register a civil marriage, and then at a later stage have a large church wedding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_East">Middle East</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Middle East">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The cohabitation rate in West Asian countries is much lower than in Europe or Latin America. In some parts of the continent it is however becoming more common for young people. As of 1994, the rate of premarital cohabitation in Israel was 25%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cohabitation is illegal according to <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">sharia</a> law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (January 2016)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It is also discouraged by the Jewish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halacha" title="Halacha">Halacha</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Australia, 22% of couples were cohabiting as of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. 78% of couples who marry have lived together beforehand in 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> rising from 16% in 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> As of 2013, of all births, 34% were to unmarried women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Australia recognizes <a href="/wiki/Australian_family_law" title="Australian family law">de facto relationships</a>. The proportion of births outside marriage varies by state/territory, being, in 2009, lowest in <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a> (at 28%), <a href="/wiki/Australian_Capital_Territory" title="Australian Capital Territory">Australian Capital Territory</a> (at 29%), and <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> (at 30%); and highest in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a> (at 63%) and <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a> (at 51%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cohabitation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In New Zealand, 23.7% of couples were cohabiting as of 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> In 2010, 48% of births were outside of marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> Like Australia, New Zealand recognizes <i>de facto</i> relationships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">High Commissioner for Human Rights <a href="/wiki/Navi_Pillay" title="Navi Pillay">Navi Pillay</a> has called for full respect and recognition of women's autonomy and sexual and reproductive health rights, stating: "Violations of women's human rights are often linked to their sexuality and reproductive role. Women are frequently treated as property, they are sold into marriage, into trafficking, into sexual slavery. (...) In many countries, married women may not refuse to have sexual relations with their husbands, and often have no say in whether they use contraception. (...) Ensuring that women have full autonomy over their bodies is the first crucial step towards achieving substantive equality between women and men. Personal issues - such as when, how and with whom they choose to have sex, and when, how and with whom they choose to have children - are at the heart of living a life in dignity."<a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.chr.up.ac.za/images/files/news/news_2012/Navi%20Pillay%20Lecture%2015%20May%202012.pdf" rel="nofollow">[1]</a></span></li>
